<td style="width:40%; max-height:1px; border-top:2px solid transparent; border-right:1px solid transparent;"></td>
<td style="width:60%; max-height:1px; border-top:2px solid transparent; border-left:1px solid transparent;"></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Methane</b> (<span class="nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">US</a></small> <span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɛ/ short 'e' in 'bed'">ɛ</span><span title="/θ/ 'th' in 'thigh'">θ</span><span title="/eɪ/ long 'a' in 'base'">eɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a></small> <span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/iː/ long 'e' in 'seed'">iː</span><span title="/θ/ 'th' in 'thigh'">θ</span><span title="/eɪ/ long 'a' in 'base'">eɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Chemical_compound" title="Chemical compound">chemical compound</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_formula" title="Chemical formula">chemical formula</a> <span class="chemf nowrap">CH<sub>4</sub></span> (one atom of <a href="/wiki/Carbon" title="Carbon">carbon</a> and four atoms of <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a>). It is a <a href="/wiki/Group_14_hydride" title="Group 14 hydride">group 14 hydride</a> and the simplest <a href="/wiki/Alkane" title="Alkane">alkane</a>, and is the main constituent of <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>. The relative abundance of methane on <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a> makes it an attractive <a href="/wiki/Fuel" title="Fuel">fuel</a>, though capturing and storing it poses challenges due to its <a href="/wiki/Gaseous" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaseous">gaseous</a> state under <a href="/wiki/Standard_conditions_for_temperature_and_pressure" title="Standard conditions for temperature and pressure">normal conditions for temperature and pressure</a>.</p>
<p>Natural methane is found both below ground and under the <a href="/wiki/Sea_floor" class="mw-redirect" title="Sea floor">sea floor</a>. When it reaches the surface and the <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Earth" title="Atmosphere of Earth">atmosphere</a>, it is known as <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_methane" title="Atmospheric methane">atmospheric methane</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The Earth's atmospheric methane concentration has increased by about 150% since 1750, and it accounts for 20% of the total <a href="/wiki/Radiative_forcing" title="Radiative forcing">radiative forcing</a> from all of the long-lived and globally mixed <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a> (these gases don't include water vapor which is by far the largest component of the <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_effect" title="Greenhouse effect">greenhouse effect</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Technical_summary_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Technical_summary-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>
