Polar clouds, made of methane, on Titan (left) compared with <a href="/wiki/Polar_stratospheric_cloud" title="Polar stratospheric cloud">polar clouds</a> on <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a> (right).</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a> – the atmosphere contains 2.3% methane<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ariel_(moon)" title="Ariel (moon)">Ariel</a> – methane is believed to be a constituent of Ariel's surface ice</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Miranda_(moon)" title="Miranda (moon)">Miranda</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oberon_(moon)" title="Oberon (moon)">Oberon</a> – about 20% of Oberon's surface ice is composed of methane-related carbon/nitrogen compounds</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Titania_(moon)" title="Titania (moon)">Titania</a> – about 20% of Titania's surface ice is composed of methane-related organic compounds<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Umbriel_(moon)" title="Umbriel (moon)">Umbriel</a> – methane is a constituent of Umbriel's surface ice</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">Neptune</a> – the atmosphere contains 1.5 ± 0.5% methane<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Triton_(moon)" title="Triton (moon)">Triton</a> – Triton has a tenuous nitrogen atmosphere with small amounts of methane near the surface.<sup id="cite_ref-nature2_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nature2-110">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-grand_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grand-111">[110]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a> – <a href="/wiki/Spectroscopic" class="mw-redirect" title="Spectroscopic">spectroscopic</a> analysis of Pluto's surface reveals it to contain traces of methane<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Solstation_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Solstation-113">[112]</a></sup>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Charon_(moon)" title="Charon (moon)">Charon</a> – methane is believed present on Charon, but it is not completely confirmed<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eris_(dwarf_planet)" title="Eris (dwarf planet)">Eris</a> – infrared light from the object revealed the presence of methane ice<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Halley%27s_Comet" title="Halley's Comet">Halley's Comet</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Comet_Hyakutake" title="Comet Hyakutake">Comet Hyakutake</a> – terrestrial observations found <a href="/wiki/Ethane" title="Ethane">ethane</a> and methane in the comet<sup id="cite_ref-science_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-science-116">[115]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Extrasolar_planet" class="mw-redirect" title="Extrasolar planet">Extrasolar planets</a> – methane was detected on extrasolar planet <a href="/wiki/HD_189733b" class="mw-redirect" title="HD 189733b">HD 189733b</a>; this is the first detection of an organic compound on a planet outside the solar system. Its origin is unknown, since the planet's high temperature (700&#160;°C) would normally favor the formation of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_monoxide" title="Carbon monoxide">carbon monoxide</a> instead.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> Research indicates that <a href="/wiki/Meteoroid" title="Meteoroid">meteoroids</a> slamming against <a href="/wiki/Extrasolar_planet" class="mw-redirect" title="Extrasolar planet">exoplanet</a> atmospheres could add hydrocarbon gases such as methane, making the exoplanets look as though they are inhabited by life, even if they are not.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Interstellar_cloud" title="Interstellar cloud">Interstellar clouds</a><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup></li>
<li>The atmospheres of <a href="/wiki/M-type_star" class="mw-redirect" title="M-type star">M-type stars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Methane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-serpentinization-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-serpentinization_54-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">There are many <a href="/wiki/Serpentinite" title="Serpentinite"><i>serpentinization</i></a> reactions. <a href="/wiki/Olivine" title="Olivine">Olivine</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Solid_solution" title="Solid solution">solid solution</a> between <a href="/wiki/Forsterite" title="Forsterite">forsterite</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fayalite" title="Fayalite">fayalite</a> whose general formula is (Fe,Mg)<sub>2</sub>SiO<sub>4</sub>. The reaction producing methane from olivine can be written as: <i>Forsterite + Fayalite + Water + Carbonic acid → Serpentine + Magnetite + Methane</i> , or (in balanced form): 18 Mg<sub>2</sub>SiO<sub>4</sub> + 6 Fe<sub>2</sub>SiO<sub>4</sub> + 26 H<sub>2</sub>O + CO<sub>2</sub> → 12 Mg<sub>3</sub>Si<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub>(OH)<sub>4</sub> + 4 Fe<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> + CH<sub>4</sub></span></li>
</ol>
</div>

<li id="cite_note-:0-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-:0_22-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-:0_22-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Cornell, Clayton B.
